  9. I purchased this safety razor a few weeks ago, and my wife and I put it through it's paces. First off, pair the 38 HD with a good quality blade (Feather or Israeli Personnas), you won't go back to disposables or cartridges. Next you'll want a good shaving soap/cream, a brush, and a good shaving bowl or cup to work up your lather. Finally, I highly recommend a pre-shave oil and a good after shave care regimen (witch hazel and Nivea sensitive skin aftershave balm (it's cheap!)).<br /><br />The weight of this razor is quite a bit more than the old Mach 3 I had been using for the past 5 years or so. The Merkur 38 HD could easily double as a hammer or personal defence tool if needed. The feel in the hand is at that sweet spot for my larger hands: heavy, a long handle that is at the proper diameter for my hand size, and the solid construction definitely puts it up there with more expensive razors. The weight pretty much guarantees a smooth, effortless shave on the face (myself) with minimal passes and effort (you don't have to apply pressure to get a good pass), since that weight and a good blade take all of the work out of shaving. When my wife used it for her legs, she noticed (like me) that the shave was much closer than the previous cartridges we had been using for so long, with a lot less touch-ups and multiple passes. We have also noted there was much less irritation and ingrown hairs after getting a grip with proper use of a safety razor (no shaving against the grain!).<br /><br />One note for the ladies that may plan on using one of these: if you plan on shaving your legs with this razor, be sure to use a thick, stiff bristle brush to work up your lather and to stand up the hairs for a better shave. My wife complained that the silvertip badger brush was too soft for her to be of any use outside of the majestic feel of the soft bristles. I'm not saying to grab a toothbrush, but you may want to look at a boar bristle or one of the cheaper Escali badger bristle brushes if you plan on shaving legs. You'll want something with a little less &#34;give&#34; and better exfoliating properties.<br /><br />So you got your razor, some good blades, an amazing brush, some soap/creame, a pre and after-shave care package: how do you clean and maintain the razor and blades? I typically disassemble my razor after use and, along with the used blade, soak them in 90%+ alcohol for around 30 minutes after a shave. This cleans and disinfects the blade and the razor's head, as well as removes any remaining soap or creame residue from between the blade and head. A quick wipe with a towel or microfiber cloth after a soak brings everything to shiny, beautiful goodness once again (never wipe your blades, shake to get most of the alcohol off) and reassemble your razor and place everything back on your razor stand until the next shave. This will keep it looking new as well as keep it clean and remove the excess water in between the blade and head (alcohol is more volatile (evaporates quickly) and sanitizes rather well).<br /><br />All in all, if you've never shaved with a safety razor, you're definitely missing out on one of the best shaves of your life (unless you take the time to learn to use a straight razor or find a barber like I did). If you want to experience a proper shave, hit up youtube and watch a few shave demonstrations, then come back and get this bad boy and get ready to knock your woman dead with that handsome baby smooth face (for you men) or completely erase your man's mind with ridiculously smooth legs (for you women). After a couple of shaves, you'll have the technique down to a proper shave each and every time, with no cuts (yes, I've actually cut myself, once when I first got it), and you'll save money for the long run (a year or more of blades will set you back around $14 or so, and whatever the cost of your soap/creame and pre/after shave products).<br /><br />Your grandparents had it right when they used these bad boys back in theday. Your dad probably learned to shave with one of these when he was younger. The cost definitely is a bit pricier up front, but you'll come out cheaper after a few months of switching from your cartridges (which can be $20 or more each month!), and have much less waste in the end (the blades are fully recyclable, and only come wrapped in paper) which makes them prime for someone who recycles at home.<br /><br />I highly recommend this razor if you have medium to large man/woman hands and want to save money over the life of this razor, since blades are so cheap and at such a higher quality, not to mention the quality of your shave is infinitely better once you have learned the proper shave technique.<br /><br />I still want to find out who in their right mind thought multi blade cartridges were better for shaving than this &#34;old&#34; tech and give them a piece of my mind....

  13. The merkur Model 38 HD Barber Pole DE Razor was the first DE Razor I used. I started wet shaving 7 weeks ago but I have been shaving with cartridge razors for a little over 35 years. First off, let me say this, compared to a few other DE razors I've purchased, vintage DE razors, this brand new DE razor made in Solingen Germany is very well made (I also own and use a DOVO straight razor made in Solingen). The heft of the razor is ideal for letting the weight of the razor shave your beard w/o adding any of your own pressure to move the razor across your face At the time I purchased this razor here at Amazon, I also bought a package of Derby Extra DE Razor blades (5 pack) and a 10 pack of Feather DE blades, also purchased here at Amazon. I highly recommend using/trying both the Derby and the Feather razor blade with this razor. Both work well with this razor with the Feather being the sharper of the two, yet the Derby will give a good close shave used in this shaver. If you buy both of the aforementioned DE razor blades, you will know what I'm talking about when I mention the Feather is sharper, and again, that does not imply the Derby blade is not sharp, it is sharp, but the Feather is very sharp and you will feel the sharpness after your shave due to more of the top layer of skin cells will be removed when using the Feather razor blade When using this or any DE Razor, you do not want to add pressure with your hand. That is a big no no. You want to let the weight of the razor cut your whiskars. Adding pressure with your hand will result in your face getting nicked or cut. This razor was designed to shave you well letting only the weight of the shaver head do the work of cutting along with your choice of razor blade. The stradegy of getting a good shave using a DE razor, unlike a cartridge razor that employs multiple blades in one throw away razor, the DE razor should be used making up to 3 passes during a shave. You make your lather, apply w/a brushand make your first pass WTG (with the grain), then rinse and re-lather. Doing your 2nd pass, you want to shave XTG (across the grain), and I'm talking about the grain or the direction which your beard grows. Typically, a lot of beards grow downwards so the WTG pass you will shave using down strokes. XTG shaving you would shave left to right or right to left. For your 3rd pass if you so choose, this pass may be ATG (against the grain), so you would shave starting anywhere on your face but using upwards strokes with the razor. So some shavers find this type of shaving pattern may cut too close to their skin, so you might find this shave pass to be uncomfortable for you, or you may find some areas of your face will not like an ATG shaving pass. Experience is the best teacher. I should mention here and now, shaving in this way using multiple passes with a DE razor accomplishes what is known as beard reduction. Your beard hairs will cut easier and more effectively if you shave them using multiple passes (from different directions), so take your time and don't hurry. Let the weight of the razor cut the hair In my opinion, when I first used this razor I was new to DE shaving, and I took my time shaving and did (always) a good face prep and was rewarded with a close shave w/o any nicking or cutting of my skin, but if I tried to hurry with this razor and got careless, it would nick here and there. Nicks and cuts can be avoided by taking your time, doing a good face prep before shaving, building a proper lather with a quality shave brush and using a good shaving soap or shaving cream, and letting the weight of the razor cut your beard, and if you want a very close shave, make sure you make multiple passes with the razor one pass at a time. Lather, shave, rinse, repeat, but shave in a different direction or pass each time If you're new to wet shaving and this will be your first DE Razor purchase, while you're waiting for the razor to arrive, take your timeand read about wet shaving at some of the various wet shaving web sites (use a search engine looking for 'wet shaving'). That way you will be prepared for your first shave having taken the time to read how it is done I highly recommend this particular razor. It has a nice hefty feel to it, the handle is long so you wont feel like you have run out of room with it in your hand, yet you can choke up on it and not use the entire length of the handle. The chrome plating is very good, and one other thing I need to mention, especially if you are a new DE Razor user....you want to make sure you tighten the handle after inserting the razor blade. This is a two piece DE Razor. The top of the head comes off when you unscrew at the very bottom of the handle. You do this so you can insert the razor blade. If you re-insert the top of the razor to the rest of the razor and do not tighten correctly, the top of the razor can allow the razor blade to move up and down, which is not good as your skin can possibly get caught between the blade and the guard (I've done this once=:-(, and got a good cut for being negligent. Don't make this rookie mistake. Make sure you always tighten the top of the razor well before using. Buy this razor with confidence as it is a fine shaving tool and one that will last you your entire life with proper use and care

  26. I've tried many DE (double-edge) razors, knowing full well that DE shaves are far closer than the multi-blade Gillettes. This is the best by far, for several reasons: Best heft and balance; best weight and length; funtional-yet-esthetic design; and an unbelievably close shave as the result. Do your due-diligence and research wet shaving -- there are a few tricks to the trade you need to know first. Here, in a nutshell, is all you need to know to get a great wet shave with this (or any) DE razor:<br /><br />1) PREP. Buy this razor and a few other preparatory items (mentioned right here). You can start with most any DE blade. Also have: Proraso shaving cream; a badger shaving brush.<br />2) LATHER. Wash face with warm water (or just take a shower), then squeeze a quarter-sized dollop of shaving cream onto the warm, wet brush; start whipping up a lather directly on your face. Use circular motions, diagonal motions, horizontal, vertical -- it doesn't matter. Get a good lather, which will be denser and less bulky than if you'd used commercial spraycan foams.<br />3) SHAVE. Slow and steady. Short strokes at all times. After a stroke or two, turn the razor over to use the clean side of the blade. Rinse and repeat. Always shave with the grain.<br />4) RELATHER; SHAVE AGAIN. Yep, that's right: Do it all over again -- but with one change: Shave across the grain. That means that after you relather, you shave from ear to nose, lobe to chin, going toward the center of the face. This is ACROSS the grain, not AGAINST the grain, and it makes the single biggest difference in going from a decent to a superbly close shave. Pay special attention to your neck: It is its own labyrinth of errant, erratic hair growth patterns. I just go after it twice, once straight down from chin to collarbone in short strokes; and once diagonally from lobe to Adam's apple. That usually gets most of it.<br /><br />I hope this helps. I went from cordless-electric-shave-in-the-car to spend-10-minutes-on-your-face-after-shower and there is no going back.<br /><br />Just remember to start slowly with short strokes. That's the only thumbrule you need. You won't regret the switch to DE shaving.here is no going back. Just remember to start slowly with short strokes. That's the only thumbrule you need. You won't regret the switch to DE shaving.

  36. This is a great razor and it is very heavy duty. I am a long-time fan of DE safety razors. I already have a Merkur VISION which I am very happy with except thoroughly cleaning/maintaining it is cumbersome. With this razor, to change the blade, you unscrew the long handle and the top blade guard easily comes off to change the blade [i.e. screwing the long handle clockwise tightens the blade assembly at the top of the razor. Cleaning is very easy. You can unscrew the handle as described above and you can also further pull the long axis of the handle to expose more parts and get a deeper clean. When reassembling the razor, be sure the reassemble the long handle by pressing the little c-clip in with your fingers to make it glide into the body of the handle. This razor is not adjustable per Se. I generally use DE razors in one position anyway. In the most tightened position, the blade is held very stable without much wiggle room. The teeth allow more contact with the skin/hair for a better shave. I have very tough and coarse facial hair but sensitive skin. What a combo. This razor in combination w/ Colonel Conk Soap, a badger brush, and Wilkinson blades gives me a relatively, surprisingly smooth and easy shave. Not luxurious like Trumper's cream but a fraction of the cost and very effective (provides more slickness to give less drag than the cream). I suggest those looking to move to wet shaving for cost reasons try the Arko stick and pick up some Nivea Sensitive Skin Post Shave Balm.   56. I'm new to DE shaving. I'm currently 25 years old, and started shaving with a Mach3 (too young for my dad to have started on one of these, so I guess I'm a pioneer of sorts in my family). After getting sick of cutting myself and the irritation I got from the Mach3, I switched to a Norelco electric razor and used that for about 6 years, but was never thrilled with the closeness of the shave. I was about to buy replacement blades for the electric when I came across these retro double-edge razors. So after some thought, I picked this razor up along with a few Derby Extra blades. I have to say, this razor is just awesome. It's nice and heavy; built like a tank. Likely built to the same standards they had back in the 1920s and 1930s. Having watched the various videos online, I had an idea of how to shave with one of these and on my first shave, I didn't cut myself once, didn't have any irritation, and had the closest shave I've ever had. The key seems to be applying no pressure, and shaving in different directions on multiple passes, removing stubble bit by bit. Whenever I used the Mach3, it felt like I was yanking out my stubble. Not so with this razor. For what it's worth, taking my time and doing multiple passes with the Mach3 didn't help - I still got the yanking feeling. I also wanted to note that I didn't buy any of the shave soaps or brushes - I've been using regular shaving cream and shaving after I shower, which is probably the most important part since that makes the hairs easier to cut. I expect to try out the soaps sooner or later, but don't feel like you need to make that leap right away. Why did I pick this particular razor? Well, after researching, I came to the conclusion that Merkur arguably makes the best DE razors on the market. This one is also a bit more forgiving on beginners (eliminating some of the more exotic models), and it had a bit of extra heft, which made it preferable to me over the HD. The internet forums also suggested this razor as a good one to make the leap into DE shaving. Just a note to fellow beginners - a lot of the experienced users of DE razors comment on how the handle of this particular razor is quite long. Indeed, compared to the Merkur HD (34C), it's a longer handle. But, compared to the Gillette cartridge razors, the handle of the 38C is about the same. If you're used to the Gillettes, I'd suggest starting with this razor since it will be less of a change for you, in addition to the extra heft making it less likely that you'll apply too much pressure.

It is heavier than the #180, and probably on the heavier side of DE razors in general. Interestingly, while my old razor's handle is diamond knurled (a cross-hatch design carved up and down the pole, rather rough on my hands), this razor is only diagonal knurled (carvings in the handle run only one direction diagonally). So this razor handle is rather smoother. This will of course affect your grip. We ladies (or anyone who doesn't do frequent manual labor) appreciate the absence of pointy diamond knurls in the #38c.<br /><br />Also, the adjustable screw in the base (non-blade edge) releases the blade assembly, allowing for greater safety and allowing one to control the level of hold over the blade. The only other razor I've used had a blade assembly that opened by twisting the whole assembly itself. That meant that if I placed too much pressure on the blade when shaving, I might twist the assembly to the side and loosen the blade. Not good! The #38c's design ensures that that won't happen.<br /><br />It's something you'd be proud to display, as compared with many more utilitarian designs (#180, I'm looking at you), and it's a great work of engineering too. Full marks!

Some people will go for: - historical collector's items - luxury razors: gold plated, ivory handled, presentation cases, etc. - gadgetry: various adjustables or clever mechanisms This razor is not for any of those people (except perhaps to fill out the collector's stable of razors). If you are looking for something that is functional, well made (well enough to last several lifetimes, probably) and good looking then you have come to the right place. This razor does have a couple of characteristics that differentiate it from other razors that the previous paragraph could just as well describe. First, it is a bit heavier than most. Whether this is right for you is a matter of personal choice. I like the heft. If you want a similar, but lighter razor try the [[ASIN:B000NL0T1G Merkur Long Handled Safety Razor - #180]]. Second, it has a longer handle than most. Again this is a matter of personal choice and perhaps the size of your hand. If you like the idea of a little extra heft but want a more traditional handle length, try the [[ASIN:B000QYEK88 Merkur Heavy Duty Double Edge Razor #34C]]. This one is so popular it has a nick-name: The \\"Merkur HD\\" (or in shaving circles simply the \\"HD\\"). If you prefer neither the extra heft nor the longer handle, go for the [[ASIN:B000S5OK9E Merkur Standard Safety Razor with Bar #33C]]. If you prefer a real \\"vintage\\" look try the [[ASIN:B001LYAQCG Merkur \\"1904\\" Safety Razor 42C]]. Merkur also makes several other styles that may or may not be available on Amazon (you'll have to Google them). One negative point (but not negative enough to knock off that fifth star): The knob on the end of the handle used to open up the razor for inserting the blade is polished smooth and a little slippery so sometimes takes a little finagling to open up. BLADES: There are many DE blades available. The few you might find in your local drug store may not be suitable. Google for \\"DE blade sampler packs choice\\" to find a sampler pack with a large variety of blades. You can decide which you like. Be sure to get one of the packs with the Feather blades. Those are my favorite (so far, it could take a year to try everything). Oh, yes, the sample blade that comes with the razor is a Merkur. Merkur makes nice razors but they are not known (at least in a positive sense) for their blades. WARNING! If you start viewing the above razors with designations like 34C, 38C and 42C, Amazon will start showing you bras and womens' dresses as suggestions based on your browsing history!

I picked one up, along with a brush and a cake of soap, and will never go back.<br /><br />ADVANTAGES:<br /> * A weeks worth of stubble, or a month's - this a single swipe will take it down to bare skin, two inches at a time - just rinse (opening the blade chamber a bit can help) and repeat. This is simply impossible to do with a multi-blade system - they will clog and become useless after half an inch.<br /> * A single blade will last 4 or 5 shaves (more, with some care). Multi-blade systems might get this many, if you are lucky, but they cost over a dollar per head. I picked up a 100 pack of Gilette DE blades for $7 - you do the math.<br /> * The blades can just be wrapped back up in the paper they come in, and thrown away - where they will rust away to nothing in the landfill. No piles of plastic, no shaving cream cans.<br /><br />Basically, what it comes down to is modern shaving tools are nothing more than a scam - they make shaving slightly easier at the expense of extremely high costs and lots of waste. With a little practice and patience (a couple weeks of practice and a few extra minutes per shave patience), a 100-year-old tech DE blade will do the same job for a tiny fraction of the cost. The razor itself is a lifetime purchase - and then you can leave it to your grandson and THEY can use it for their lifetime. Ifyou want to go even further back and save even more money, you can get a straight razor and strop, but those are a little too scary for me. ;)

It has heft that means business and reeks high quality.<br /> While I am fairly new to safety and straight razor shaving, I do also own the Merkur 180 (aka the 23c), the Merkur Futur, the Edwin Jagger DE89L and a Thiers Issard straight. While I am practicing and learning with all the razors (especially the Thiers), the Merkur 38 HD is my daily go to beard cutter. This razor is a two piece unit which I really like and you unscrew the bottom of the handle to remove the top and put in a new blade. I also am very fond of the barber pole texture on the handle which helps me hold the razor when it is wet. (How did you miss this when designing the Futur, Merkur?) The blade gap on this razor is 0.64 mm which is neither aggressive or weak. And the Merkur 38 HD seems to have just the right design to reach everywhere on my face except right under the nostrils. Slap a Feather blade in this bad boy and it will cut any beard like butter.<br /> Overall, I would give the 38c HD about 4.8 stars out of five. If I could redesign it, my only addition would be a slightly longer handle (I would have made it about 125 mm long). Despite this minor flaw, shaving with the 38c HD makes me feel like I am going to meet Winston Churchill for a War Cabinet meeting. When connoisseurs of fine products speak of items where form intersects function with aesthetic appeal, the Merkur 38c HD is an example of what they mean.

  302. EDIT (3 years later): I've been using this razor for about 3 years now. I am STILL using the same box of razors, though the shave soap ran out long ago. The soap dish and brush stand are still working fine, and the shave brush is also still in very good shape. I still dry the blade and razor after each use (maybe 2-3 shaves per week), and the blades are very consistently lasting between 5 and 7 shaves, depending on the thickness of the hair growth. This means, as you'll see in the post farther down, I am still YEARS away from using up the box of 100 blades I originally purchased. Very happy with this razor, and I would still recommend it to anyone looking for a great safety razor with a great look, great lines, and superior engineering.<br /><br />ORIGINAL REVIEW STARTS HERE:<br /><br />I've used cartridge razors for years. I've gone from single-bladed cartridge or disposable razors all the way up to 3 and 4 bladed cartridges. I've used electric razors and even tried depilatories. With all of those, I have suffered with consistent irritation and trouble with shaving bumps. Evidently, I have sensitive skin, especially on my neck.<br /><br />I purchased the Model 38 HD a bit over a week ago. I received it in the mail and loaded it with the included Merkur razor blade. I also bought some [[ASIN:B00008X5CH Williams Mug Shaving Soap - 1.75 oz]]. I put a light lather of the soap on my face, and began to shave with the 38 HD. I was immediately amazed at how smooth the save was, even though my beard was about 4 days heavy. The razor cuts the way a razor should cut, without snagging or pulling at the hair. An added bonus that I found was the accuracy with which I can shape my beard and mustache, since the one blade is extremely narrow. After the shave, splashing on some cold water finished the experience off nicely. It was the best shave I've had in years, and when I say years, I mean like 25 years.<br /><br />I've seen reviewers talk about the extended length of time it takes to shave, or the nicks and cuts they get from using a Merkur safety razor. My very first shave took about 5 minutes less than it usually does with a cartridge razor. I had one very small nick on my neck, probably due to a small pimple or something there that I didn't notice. With the Williams Mug Shaving Soap, the razor glides as though it had its own comfort strip attached. It is extremely difficult to cut yourself with this razor as long as you shave like a normal human being and don't try to hack away at your face. I'm confident that it will give you a very special and irritation free shaving experience. I will never go back to the cartridge razor, and I'm actually thinking of purchasing this along with shaving equipment as a gift for some of my family and friends. It has impressed me that much. I am, however, looking at trying out a Dovo Straight Razor next. I received a straight razor shave one time in the military in Japan, and it was also a great experience. I will also review that when I have developed an opinion about the experience.<br /><br />The Model 38 HD is an elegant piece of hardware. It is well-designed and feels well-made in the hand. The weight of the razor lends itself to the ease of the shave, since the razor is heavy enough to basically cut through the hair on its own. The smooth chrome of the blade cover doesn't irritate or drag the skin as long as the skin is soaped and wet, but will catch a little as the skin dries out, which is expected with polished metal. The blade is clamped to a comfortable curvature, which helps the blades stiffness and keeps the edge steady against the hair during the cutting process. This razor is a great piece of equipment, and I am thoroughly pleased with it.<br /><br />One tip I would give: When finished with the shave, remove the blade and, using a clean paper towel or cloth, clean the razor blade thoroughly along with the razor. Slip the razor blade back into the razor and tighten the mechanism down on the blade before storing it OUTSIDE OF THE BATHROOM, perhaps in the bedroom or a closet. By keeping the razor blade dry and stored outside the bathroom away from steam and moisture, the blade should last quite a bit longer, and so be even more cost-effective.<br /><br />I fully recommend this razor and the blades by Merkur (though I also use [[ASIN:B0077LAJT2 Personna Double Edge Razor Blades]] , which are also extremely cost-effective and outstanding razor blades. I think anyone that uses this razor in a reasonable fashion will be instantly hooked.<br /><br />Congratulations, Merkur, on producing a fantastic piece of shaving equipment.<br /><br />EDIT: So, I've been shaving with this razor now for about a week, and I still couldn't be more pleased. Shaving irritation is down, shaving bumps are disappearing, and I'm still using the same blade that came with the razor. I did the math on this, just to give those that may be curious an idea of the savings with this equipment. I purchased my complete setup for around $122 including shipping. I bought the 38HD Classic, Personna Blades (100 in a pack), Tweezerman's Badger Hair Brush, Williams shaving soap, a soap bowl, and a brush stand. If I use the blades as I stated above, I'm getting at least seven shaves out of each blade. That gives me 700 shaves with one box of razors. Comparing that to the Mach3 cartridge razors, I spend about $25 on eight blades, and get around three shaves per cartridge. That comes to about $1.04 per shave. At that cost, using the Merkur would have cost around $728, just for the razor blades alone, so about $783 for the razor and blades. The razor and the blades ran me a bit over $70 with shipping, which comes to about 10 cents per shave. Even with the other equipment (stand, bowl, soap, and brush), I'm still averaging about 17 cents per shave. That is over 6.12 times cheaper than using cartridges. Anyone still need convincing? I'm 38, and if I live to be 70 (32 more years) I will only replenish my blade supply about 16.7 more times, at a current cost of around $16.00. That comes to about $266.97 over the next 32 years for the blades alone. If I use cartridges, according to my math (which could be mistaken....feel free to check the numbers), I will have to replenish my cartridge razor supply 486.7 times, and at $25.00 a package at today's cost, that equates to about $12,166.67 for the cartridges alone. That's more expensive than the Merkur over 32 years by a factor of 45. The savings just grow as you get older. Anyone have any questions, feel free to message me.   303. I started my DE shaving adventure with a Merkur 38C HD razor (3 inch handle). I used this alone for just over 4 months and I really like it. The only thing that wasn't perfect for my particular set of conditions was it was a little difficult to see clearly past my hand when shaving the edge of my long left side burn. I am right- handed and the shorter handle made it more difficult to get my hand back far enough to assure I was creating a straight edge for my entire sideburn. Shaving the right sideburn was not as much of an issue with my right hand. And the rest of my shaving with the smaller handled razor was just fine.<br /><br />I eventually decided to get this Barber Pole Merkur HD as I thought the extra 3/4 inch long handle would be perfect for moving my hand back a little more while shaving so I could see the full left sideburn edge. Before purchasing this I verified that it also had only 2 sectional pieces for removing/inserting blades. The only small difference I see between the shorter Merkur Hd and this Barber Pole version besides the slightly longer handle is that the Barber Pole version also has handle grip grooves that are cut a bit less deeply into the handle and there is a more aesthetically rounded bottom tip (Barber Pole like) instead of the knurled knob at the base of the smaller 38C model. The perfect razor for me would be the 38C HD with the Barber Pole length handle, but this Barber Pole works just fine.<br /><br />The grip is still quite adequate and not slippery and there have been no issues loosening/tightening the bottom knob to change blades. Gentle finger tightening works quite well in securing the blade. And you should always be changing blades with a dry razor and hands anyway.<br /><br /> I see no change in shaving aggressiveness from its original little brother, Merkur 38C HD. So I am quite happy with this purchase. The slightly longer handle does actually allow me to move my hand back just enough to see the left sideburn edge betterand shave a straighter edge there. This Barber Pole also has that similar solid feel and weight that I got and liked from the shorter Merkur razor. I therefore will be keeping both of these Merkur razors in my arsenal. They are both well-made and should last me a very, very long time. Although everyone is different, for the most part I think the choice between the longer and shorter versions of the Merkur line should be mainly based on which suits your own particular shaving needs better. Good luck with your future in DE shaving.
